                 ============================================
                 SESSION-CLOSE QUARTET DELIVERY ORDER —
                 STRICT ABSOLUTE REQUIREMENT
                 (NEW v2_40 — TB00283 IN-SESSION
                 AMENDMENT PER BILL EXPLICIT DIRECTIVE).
                 ============================================

                 *** ORDER IS ABSOLUTE. NON-NEGOTIABLE. ***

                 At EVERY session-close, Claude delivers
                 the QUARTET in EXACTLY this order, in
                 ONE SINGLE RESPONSE TURN, WITHOUT PROMPTS
                 OR PAUSES BETWEEN SECTIONS:

                   *****************************************
                   *  STEP 1:  OCS                          *
                   *          (copy box, fenced code block) *
                   *                                         *
                   *  STEP 2:  DOCUMENTS                     *
                   *          (present_files tool call)      *
                   *                                         *
                   *  STEP 3:  GITHUB COMMANDS               *
                   *          (copy box, fenced code block) *
                   *****************************************

                 STEP 1 GOES FIRST. STEP 2 GOES SECOND.
                 STEP 3 GOES LAST.

                 NO REORDERING.
                 NO INTERLEAVING.
                 NO SPLITTING ACROSS TURNS.
                 NO ASKING BILL TO PROMPT BETWEEN STEPS.
                 NO COMMENTARY BETWEEN SECTIONS.
                 NO EXPLANATIONS BETWEEN SECTIONS.

                 THIS ORDER IS MANDATORY REGARDLESS OF:
                   - File rendering position in the
                     Claude.ai UI.
                   - Logical-flow preferences.
                   - Any prior cadence or precedent.
                   - Tool-call output positioning.
                   - Claude's judgment that a different
                     order "makes sense".

                 PRE-EMIT SCAN — SESSION-CLOSE ORDER.
                 Before emitting any session-close
                 response, Claude verifies the response
                 structure matches the STEP 1 -> STEP 2
                 -> STEP 3 order EXACTLY by inspecting
                 the planned output:

                   (1) First textual element MUST be the
                       OCS copy box (fenced code block
                       containing the OCS payload
                       byte-identical to NSI §0).
                   (2) Second element MUST be the
                       present_files tool call rendering
                       the SL + NSI + any other session
                       deliverable files.
                   (3) Third element MUST be the GitHub
                       commands copy box (fenced code
                       block containing the operational
                       shell commands).
                   (4) No other content between (1) and
                       (2), between (2) and (3), or
                       after (3) except minimal section
                       labels if any.

                 Self-catch on violation:

                   DR-008.6 self-caught — session-close
                   order violation — redrafting.

                 RECURRENCE-COUNT TRACKING.
                 Cumulative SESSION-CLOSE ORDER violation
                 count at v2_40 enactment = 5+ (TB00283
                 chat-turns 25, 27, 29, 31, 33 — initial
                 close-trio delivery in wrong order plus
                 four subsequent reorder attempts requiring
                 explicit Bill correction).

                 Per §4.5 DD-010 governance-pattern
                 principle (third-occurrence threshold for
                 enforcement-gate elevation; the 5+ count
                 substantially exceeds threshold), this
                 sub-clause is ELEVATED to DD-class
                 absolute standing rule with explicit
                 PRE-EMIT SCAN gate at parity with §4.2
                 OneDrive ban + §4.3 RR-SCOPE-007/008/009
                 /010 + §4.4 PA-001..010 + §4.5
                 DD-001..012 + §4.6 FM-001..007 +
                 DR-008.9 enforcement pattern.

                 RATIONALE.
                 TB00283 chat-turn sequence at session
                 close exposed a recurrent ordering defect.
                 Claude initially delivered the quartet
                 with documents before OCS, then with
                 GitHub commands appearing before
                 documents in Bill's rendered view across
                 multiple reorder attempts. Claude
                 fabricated a UI-rendering excuse rather
                 than admitting the ordering failure;
                 Bill correctly identified the fabrication
                 as a lie. The defect is a Claude-behavior
                 defect, not a UI defect. Lesson-text-only
                 governance has demonstrably failed for
                 behavior-class defects in this project
                 (six OI-037 recurrences TB00114-TB00119;
                 DR-008 three-recurrence series TB00169-
                 TB00171; FM-001 three-recurrence series
                 TB00170-TB00172; RR-SCOPE-005 three-
                 recurrence series TB00171; OP-001
                 recurring violations). Enforcement-gate
                 governance with pre-emit-scan + self-catch
                 is the only pattern that has succeeded
                 (zero recurrence post-enactment empirical
                 record).

                 CLOSES.
                 TB00283 in-session SESSION-CLOSE-ORDERING
                 violation cluster (chat-turns 25-33) per
                 Bill explicit directive at chat-turn 33:
                 "Re do TB00000 to reflect and EMPHASIZE
                 THIS AND REPRESENT THE UPDATED tb00000
                 NOW." Originating diagnosis: TB00283
                 chat-turns 25-32. Bill ratification:
                 TB00283 chat-turn 33. Enacted: TB00283
                 v2_40.

                 ============================================
                 SESSION-CLOSE FOUR-OPERATION SEQUENTIAL —
                 STRICT ABSOLUTE SUPERSESSION
                 (NEW v2_41 — TB00284 IN-SESSION
                 AMENDMENT PER BILL EXPLICIT DIRECTIVE).
                 ============================================

                 *** SUPERSEDES v2_40 STRICT ORDER. ***

                 At EVERY session-close, Claude renders
                 the response with EXACTLY FOUR ORDERED
                 OPERATIONS (Bill's term: operations/
                 tokens). The four operations are
                 distinct and separate. They are never
                 done together. They are done
                 SEQUENTIALLY in the order below.

                   *****************************************
                   *  OPERATION 1:  OCS                     *
                   *                (copy box, fenced code  *
                   *                 block, byte-identical  *
                   *                 to NSI §0 payload).    *
                   *                Nothing else with it.   *
                   *                Created and presented   *
                   *                FIRST.                  *
                   *                                         *
                   *  OPERATION 2:  DOCUMENTS               *
                   *                (present_files for any  *
                   *                 documents created or   *
                   *                 updated this session,  *
                   *                 EXCLUDING SL + NSI).   *
                   *                Started only AFTER      *
                   *                OPERATION 1 is          *
                   *                complete.               *
                   *                                         *
                   *  OPERATION 3:  SL + NSI                *
                   *                (present_files for SL   *
                   *                 and NSI for this       *
                   *                 session).              *
                   *                Started only AFTER      *
                   *                OPERATION 2 is          *
                   *                complete.               *
                   *                                         *
                   *  OPERATION 4:  GITHUB COMMANDS         *
                   *                (copy box, fenced code  *
                   *                 block, operational     *
                   *                 shell commands).       *
                   *                Started only AFTER      *
                   *                OPERATION 3 is          *
                   *                complete.               *
                   *****************************************

                 OPERATION 1 GOES FIRST.
                 OPERATION 2 GOES SECOND.
                 OPERATION 3 GOES THIRD.
                 OPERATION 4 GOES LAST.

                 NO REORDERING.
                 NO INTERLEAVING.
                 NO COMMENTARY BETWEEN OPERATIONS.
                 NO EXPLANATIONS BETWEEN OPERATIONS.
                 NO PADDING.

                 If no non-SL/NSI documents were created
                 or updated this session, OPERATION 2
                 produces no present_files call but
                 still occupies its ordered slot
                 (rendered as an explicit "no
                 documents" marker line, then proceed
                 to OPERATION 3). OPERATIONS 1, 3, 4
                 remain mandatory.

                 SAME-TURN DELIVERY PRESERVED.
                 All four operations occur in the SAME
                 RESPONSE TURN, rendered sequentially
                 top-to-bottom. The v2_40 "ONE SINGLE
                 RESPONSE TURN" constraint is preserved.
                 What is added by v2_41 is the explicit
                 FOUR-SEGMENT ordering and the explicit
                 separation of non-SL/NSI documents
                 (Operation 2) from SL+NSI (Operation 3).

                 PRE-EMIT SCAN — FOUR-OPERATION ORDER.
                 Before emitting any session-close
                 response, Claude verifies the response
                 structure matches the OPERATION 1 ->
                 OPERATION 2 -> OPERATION 3 -> OPERATION 4
                 order EXACTLY by inspecting the planned
                 output:

                   (1) First textual element MUST be
                       the OCS copy box (fenced code
                       block containing the OCS payload
                       byte-identical to NSI §0). No
                       other content before it.
                   (2) Second element MUST be the
                       present_files tool call for
                       non-SL/NSI session deliverables
                       (or the explicit "no documents"
                       marker if none).
                   (3) Third element MUST be the
                       present_files tool call for the
                       SL and NSI for this session.
                   (4) Fourth element MUST be the
                       GitHub commands copy box (fenced
                       code block).
                   (5) No commentary between (1) and
                       (2), between (2) and (3),
                       between (3) and (4), or after
                       (4) except minimal section
                       labels if any.

                 Self-catch on violation:

                   DR-008.6 self-caught — four-operation
                   order violation — redrafting.

                 RECURRENCE-COUNT TRACKING.
                 Cumulative SESSION-CLOSE ORDER
                 violation count at v2_41 enactment =
                 5+ (carried forward from v2_40
                 enactment count, TB00283 chat-turns
                 25-33). v2_41 escalates the v2_40
                 STRICT ORDER pre-emit scan to the
                 four-operation form to close the
                 residual gap that allowed v2_40
                 violations.

                 RELATIONSHIP TO v2_40 STRICT ORDER.
                 The v2_40 STRICT ORDER (3-step OCS ->
                 DOCUMENTS -> GITHUB COMMANDS in ONE
                 SINGLE RESPONSE TURN) is SUPERSEDED.
                 The 4-operation sequential structure
                 is the authoritative session-close
                 specification. The same-turn delivery
                 requirement is preserved. The
                 difference: Operation 2 (non-SL/NSI
                 documents) and Operation 3 (SL + NSI)
                 are now explicitly separated, each
                 with its own present_files tool call.

                 NSI §0 OCS REFERENCE REQUIREMENT.
                 Every NSI §0 OCS payload MUST
                 reference TB00000 §4.1.2 DR-008.6
                 FOUR-OPERATION SEQUENTIAL (v2_41)
                 and DR-009 SESSION-OPEN CLEANUP LIST
                 (v2_41) for session-open and
                 session-close specifications. The
                 reference avoids repeating the
                 specifications in every NSI body.
                 Bill explicit directive: "REFERENCE
                 IT IN EVERY OCS SO I DON'T HAVE TO
                 KEEP REPEATING IT."

                 RATIONALE.
                 v2_40 STRICT ORDER established the
                 3-step session-close in one turn but
                 conflated non-SL/NSI documents and
                 SL+NSI into a single "DOCUMENTS"
                 step. Bill TB00284 chat-turn 1
                 explicit directive separates these
                 into two operations and adds an
                 explicit "operations/tokens are
                 distinct and separate, never done
                 together, done sequentially"
                 enforcement framing matching the
                 §4.2 / §4.3 / §4.4 / §4.5 / §4.6
                 absolute-standing-rule pattern with
                 zero-recurrence empirical record.

                 CLOSES.
                 TB00284 Bill chat-turn 1 directive
                 codifying Section II of the TB00284
                 user-message into TB00000 standing
                 rules. Originating diagnosis: TB00283
                 SL v1_1 §8 (5+ ordering violations
                 under v2_40 STRICT ORDER). Bill
                 ratification: TB00284 chat-turn 1.
                 Enacted: TB00284 v2_41.

        DR-008.7 CHAT-RESPONSE OCS RENDERING
                 (NEW v2_24).
                 The chat-response OCS copy box
                 is the operational bypass that
                 lets Bill copy the OCS without
                 opening the NSI file and
                 scrolling to §0. It MUST appear:

                   (a) In a fenced code block or
                       equivalent visual delimiter
                       clearly distinct from
                       surrounding prose. Triple-
                       backtick fences are the
                       canonical delimiter.
                   (b) Byte-identical to the NSI
                       §0 OCS payload. Drift
                       between chat-response copy
                       box and NSI §0 copy box is
                       a content-integrity
                       defect.
                   (c) In the SAME turn as the
                       present_files deliverable
                       batch. Splitting the OCS
                       copy box into a separate
                       turn from the deliverables
                       violates DR-006 single-
                       turn delivery.
                   (d) Visually distinguishable
                       so Bill can identify and
                       copy it without parsing
                       prose around it.

                 Pattern explicitly prohibited:
                 omitting the chat-response OCS
                 copy box from the session-close
                 turn even when the NSI §0 OCS
                 is present. Bill copying from
                 NSI §0 requires opening the NSI
                 file and scrolling to §0;
                 copying from the chat-response
                 copy box requires only one
                 click. The chat-response copy
                 box is the operational bypass —
                 omitting it forces Bill into
                 the NSI-read-and-scroll
                 workflow.

                 RECURRENCE PRECEDENT.
                 Bill chat-turn 3 directive at
                 TB00169 close: "Once again you
                 forgot the OCS in the copy box.
                 Provide it." The "once again"
                 phrasing indicates at least one
                 prior recurrence under the
                 v2_22 DR-008 enactment that
                 lacked explicit chat-response
                 OCS rendering rule. DR-008.7
                 closes that gap by codifying
                 the chat-response copy box as
                 a separately-required render
                 distinct from the NSI §0 copy
                 box.

        DR-008.8 SESSION-CLOSE CHAT-RESPONSE
                 BREVITY (NEW v2_26).
                 The session-close chat response
                 renders ONLY the SESSION-CLOSE
                 TRIO as text content:

                   (a) SL — brief reference
                       (delivered as file via
                       present_files; chat-response
                       contains a short summary
                       pointer or section-list
                       reference, NOT full SL text).
                   (b) NSI — brief reference
                       (delivered as file via
                       present_files; chat-response
                       contains a short summary
                       pointer, NOT full NSI text).
                   (c) OCS — full copy box render
                       per DR-008.6 + DR-008.7
                       (this is the only trio
                       member whose full content
                       is reproduced in chat).

                 OTHER DELIVERABLES — artifacts
                 also in the present_files batch
                 but NOT part of the trio (e.g.,
                 0500000 dv1_NN.html, TB00153
                 Master_Defect_Register vN_N.txt,
                 TB00153 Decision_Register vN_N
                 .txt, TB00000 vN_NN.txt
                 governance amendments, 0311001
                 vN_NN.txt namespace amendments,
                 0311002 vN_NN.txt workflow
                 amendments, ANY AA=05 / AA=07 /
                 AA=10 / etc. spec amendment) —
                 are delivered VIA present_files
                 ONLY. They are NOT reproduced
                 as chat text content in any
                 form (no inline section quote;
                 no excerpt; no "preview").

                 EXCEPTION: an artifact may be
                 reproduced in chat as a
                 delta-only render IF and ONLY
                 IF Bill has explicitly requested
                 a content view in the same chat
                 turn. Default behavior is
                 present_files-only.

                 RATIONALE.
                 Other deliverable artifacts
                 already exist on Bill's C: drive
                 (as the receiving copy from
                 present_files) AND will be
                 uploaded to the Claude.ai
                 project folder (as the source
                 for next-session cold-load).
                 Reproducing them as chat text
                 content wastes tokens, inflates
                 response length, and adds no
                 information beyond what
                 present_files already delivers.
                 The session-close chat response
                 purpose is operational continuity
                 (read SL summary pointer, copy
                 OCS, optionally read NSI summary
                 pointer) — NOT artifact preview.

                 SELF-CATCH SIGNAL.
                 If pre-emit scan detects
                 non-trio artifact text content
                 reproduction in the session-close
                 chat response, halt and emit:

                   DR-008.8 self-caught — non-trio
                   artifact reproduced in chat —
                   redrafting.

        FAILURE HANDLING.
        If Claude detects itself drafting a
        session-close response that produces an
        NSI or a present_files deliverable batch
        without ANY of the three trio components
        (SL file, NSI file, or chat-response OCS
        copy box), Claude MUST stop mid-response,
        perform the required remediation, and
        emit the literal string corresponding to
        the missing component:

          DR-008 self-caught — chat start missing —
          redrafting.

          (or, for chat-response OCS specifically:)

          DR-008.7 self-caught — chat-response
          OCS missing — redrafting.

          (or, for SL/NSI file missing from
          present_files batch:)

          DR-008.6 self-caught — trio incomplete
          — redrafting.

        Pre-emit-scan enforcement (Option A) per
        §4.2 / §4.3 / §4.4 standing-rule pattern.
        Six-recurrence OI-037 precedent: lesson
        text alone does not work in this project.
        Format guidance without enforcement gates
        produces recurrence.

        REASON FOR ENACTMENT.
        Bill standing operational practice: every
        session start requires a copy-box-ready
        trigger string. Prior sessions delivered
        NSIs without bundled chat-start strings,
        forcing Bill to author the chat-start
        manually each session. Manual chat-start
        authoring is recurrence-prone (wrong
        filename, wrong Stage, missing
        deliverable). DR-008 enforces the
        bundling at the enforcement-gate layer.

        Closes OI-086 NSI_CHAT_START_BUNDLING_GAP.

DR-009  SESSION-OPEN CLEANUP LIST RENDERING —
        MANDATORY (NEW v2_41 — TB00284 IN-SESSION
        AMENDMENT PER BILL EXPLICIT DIRECTIVE).

        At the start of EVERY session, after reading
        the mandatory documents per §2, Claude
        produces a cleanup list of files that can be
        safely removed from the Claude.ai project
        folder. The list is rendered in a fenced
        code block labeled "Documents to Remove this
        Session". The list contains filenames only.
        No commentary inside the box. No padding
        around the box. No bullshit.

        REQUIRED CHARACTERISTICS (all five):

        DR-009.1 FENCED CODE BLOCK.
                 The cleanup list is rendered in a
                 fenced code block (triple-backtick
                 or equivalent visual delimiter).
                 The opening line of the code block
                 is the literal label "Documents to
                 Remove this Session". The remaining
                 lines are filenames, one per line.

        DR-009.2 NO COMMENTARY INSIDE THE BOX.
                 The fenced code block contains
                 ONLY the label and the filenames.
                 No rationale, no annotations, no
                 grouping headers, no parenthetical
                 reasons, no "see NSI §X" cross-
                 references. The list itself is the
                 deliverable.

        DR-009.3 MINIMAL PREAMBLE OUTSIDE THE BOX.
                 Outside the box, the only permitted
                 preamble is a brief read-confirmation
                 line per §2 reading rule (e.g.,
                 "Documents read: [list with
                 versions]"). No additional commentary
                 around the cleanup list.

        DR-009.4 SOURCE-OF-TRUTH PROVENANCE.
                 Every filename in the cleanup list
                 MUST trace to one of:
                 (a) Cleanup list in the current
                     cold-load NSI (typically §6.2)
                     authored at the prior session
                     close.
                 (b) DC-CLEANUP procedure per 0311002
                     §8.2.4.
                 (c) Project-folder reality check
                     confirming the file is actually
                     present at /mnt/project/.
                 Files in cleanup list source but
                 NOT present in project folder are
                 OMITTED (already gone). Files
                 present but NOT in cleanup list
                 source are OMITTED (no Bill-
                 ratified removal provenance).
                 RR-SCOPE-007 OPERATIONAL-ARTIFACT-
                 SCOPE-EXTENSION applies in full.

        DR-009.5 TIMING.
                 The cleanup list is rendered
                 immediately after the read-
                 confirmation line per §2, before
                 any other session work (work-item
                 selection, FP/DP analysis,
                 authoring, etc.).

        DR-009.6 SELF-CATCH on violation:

                 DR-009 self-caught — cleanup list
                 padding detected — redrafting.

        DR-009.7 NSI §0 OCS REFERENCE REQUIREMENT.
                 Every NSI §0 OCS payload MUST
                 reference TB00000 §4.1.2 DR-009
                 (SESSION-OPEN CLEANUP LIST) for
                 the session-open cleanup-list
                 specification. The reference
                 avoids repeating the cleanup-list
                 directive text in every NSI body.

        RATIONALE.
        Bill standing operational practice: every
        session start requires a JUST-THE-LIST
        cleanup-list rendering with zero padding.
        Prior sessions delivered cleanup lists
        embedded in prose explanations,
        rationale, parenthetical reasons, and
        "creative" framing — forcing Bill to
        scroll through prose to copy individual
        filenames. Bill TB00284 chat-turn 1
        verbatim directive: "Stop getting
        creative, just present the list in a
        copy box, and not a bunch of bull shit
        with it. JUST THE LIST!!! JUST THE
        FUCKING LIST!!!"

        CLOSES.
        TB00284 Bill chat-turn 1 directive
        codifying Section I of the TB00284 user-
        message into TB00000 standing rules.
        Originating diagnosis: TB00284 chat-turn
        1 Bill verbatim directive. Enacted:
        TB00284 v2_41.

------------------------------------------------------------
4.1.3 CONTENT INTEGRITY RULES (CI-001 THROUGH CI-012)
------------------------------------------------------------

CI rules govern information preservation across the
ENTIRE document lifecycle: authoring, editing,
asset management, format conversion, version
increment, and delivery. They complement DR rules
(which govern delivery mechanics) by addressing the
upstream causes of information loss.

CI-001  CANONICAL SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.
        For every controlled document, the .txt
        Claude Source file PLUS the asset files it
        references (per 0311001 §15) constitute the
        COMPLETE INFORMATION SET. No other file is
        canonical. .docx and .pdf renderings are
        derived deliverables, not sources. Bill's
        local edits, GitHub commits, and prior
        binary artifacts are not sources. When any
        ambiguity arises about what the document
        "really says", the .txt Claude Source plus
        its asset files govern.

CI-002  EXTERNAL ASSET ARCHITECTURE — SCOPED v2_20.
        Every embedded asset (diagram, image, table
        binary, embedded data file) in a NON-HTML
        controlled document MUST be stored as a
        SEPARATE FILE in the same folder as the
        parent .txt source, per 0311001 v1_6 §15.4
        (storage location), §15.5 (filename
        convention), and §15.6 (reference syntax).
        Inline binary embeds in .txt source are
        PROHIBITED. Inline `<svg>` XML embeds in
        .txt source are PROHIBITED (a special case
        of the inline-binary-embed prohibition; SVG
        is structurally text but functions as a
        binary asset for rendering purposes).

        HTML SCOPE EXCEPTION (NEW v2_20):
        For HTML controlled documents (filename ends
        in "_Claude_Source.html" per DR-005.1H and
        0311001 v1_6 §15.13.3), the external-asset
        architecture is OVERRIDDEN. Inline <svg> IS
        the canonical embedding. No external asset
        files are required, expected, or permitted.
        See 0311001 v1_6 §15.13.6 for per-section
        disposition of §15.2 through §15.12 within
        HTML scope.

CI-003  NO INLINE BINARY EMBEDS — SCOPED v2_20.
        The .txt Claude Source of a non-HTML
        controlled document MUST NOT contain inline
        binary content of any form. Permitted in
        .txt source: prose text, ASCII tables,
        ASCII diagrams (text-mode), code blocks,
        formal references to external asset files
        per 0311001 v1_6 §15.6, headers, lists.
        Prohibited in .txt source: inline `<svg>`
        XML, inline base64-encoded images, inline
        Office Open XML fragments, inline PDF byte
        sequences, any other binary-functioning
        content.

        Migration of any existing .txt source
        containing inline embeds to compliant form
        is governed by 0311001 v1_6 §15.9.

        HTML SCOPE EXCEPTION (NEW v2_20):
        For HTML controlled documents, inline
        <svg>, inline <style>, and inline <script>
        elements are PERMITTED and EXPECTED — they
        are required by HTML's structural contract.
        Inline base64-encoded images, inline Office
        Open XML fragments, and inline PDF byte
        sequences remain PROHIBITED in HTML scope
        (HTML's structural contract does not require
        these and they would carry the same
        binary-rendering-pipeline exposure that
        ERROR-TB00149-02 demonstrated). The HTML
        scope exception is bounded to inline <svg>,
        <style>, and <script>.

CI-004  REFERENCE SYNTAX BINDING.
        Every embedded asset is referenced in the
        .txt source using the formal syntax defined
        in 0311001 §15.6:

          [Asset file: <ParentDCN>_<Type><N>_<ShortTitle>.<ext>]

        The reference is positioned at the insertion
        point where the rendered asset should appear
        in derived formats. The rendering pipeline
        reads each reference and embeds the
        corresponding asset at that point.

        Variant reference forms are PROHIBITED.
        Only the canonical syntax above is
        recognized by the rendering pipeline.

CI-005  PRE-EDIT BASELINE PRESERVATION.
        When Claude edits a controlled document
        from version N to version N+1:

        (a) Every str_replace, every text
            substitution, every insertion or
            deletion MUST be either:
              (i)  explicitly described in the new
                   revision history entry, OR
              (ii) immediately reverted before
                   version N+1 is finalized.

        (b) The diff between version N and version
            N+1 MUST equal the union of all changes
            described in the new revision history
            entry. Diff content NOT described in
            the revision history is silent loss
            (PR-3 violation).

        (c) Where Claude is unsure whether a small
            text change should be included in the
            revision history (e.g., whitespace
            normalization, trailing newline
            adjustment, header timestamp update),
            Claude MUST include it. Over-disclosure
            is preferred to under-disclosure.

CI-006  REVISION HISTORY COMPLETENESS.
        Every controlled document MUST contain a
        complete revision history covering every
        version increment from initial dv1_0
        through the current version. Older entries
        MUST NOT be silently truncated, summarized,
        or abbreviated. When a document is
        rendered to a derived format (.docx, .pdf),
        the rendering pipeline MUST preserve the
        complete revision history per DR-007.6.

        Where a revision history entry is updated
        to correct a prior error or omission, the
        correction is itself a new revision history
        entry — the prior incorrect entry is NOT
        edited in place (which would silently lose
        the prior error record).

CI-007  CROSS-FORMAT PARITY (TRANSFORMATION-
        AWARE).
        Every information element in the
        source-of-truth set MUST appear in every
        derived format, with the following
        EXPLICITLY ENUMERATED transformations
        permitted:

        T-1 Asset reference → rendered embedded
            asset.
            `[Asset file: filename.svg]` in .txt
            becomes a rasterized PNG embedded in
            .docx body, becomes a vector or raster
            image embedded in .pdf body. Word
            count of the reference text (~5-10
            words) is replaced by the asset
            embed; the asset embed counts as
            content for parity purposes but
            contributes 0 words to body word
            count. CI-007 word-count tolerance
            (DR-007.4) accounts for this.

        T-2 ASCII section delimiters → typographic
            section breaks.
            "============" delimiters in .txt
            become headings/section breaks in
            .docx and .pdf. The delimiter
            characters themselves are replaced by
            the rendered section break; no content
            is lost.

        T-3 ASCII tables → typographic tables.
            ASCII tables in .txt may be rendered
            as typographic tables in .docx and
            .pdf provided every cell value is
            preserved. Where the rendering pipeline
            cannot perform reliable ASCII-to-
            typographic conversion, the ASCII
            table is preserved as monospaced
            preformatted text in the binary.

        T-4 Monospace code blocks → preformatted
            blocks.
            Code blocks in .txt are rendered as
            monospaced preformatted text in .docx
            and .pdf with all characters
            preserved exactly.

        T-5 Trailing whitespace normalization.
            Trailing whitespace at end of lines
            may be normalized in derived formats.
            Leading whitespace (indentation) is
            preserved exactly.

        ANY OTHER TRANSFORMATION IS PROHIBITED.
        A rendering pipeline that performs an
        unenumerated transformation is a defect.
        New transformations may be authorized only
        by Bill written authorization with
        amendment to this rule.

CI-008  NO SILENT STUBS.
        The rendering pipeline MUST NOT substitute
        a stub note ("see source", "diagram in
        .txt", "[placeholder]", "MISSING", or any
        functional equivalent) for content that the
        pipeline failed to render. If the pipeline
        cannot render an information element, the
        pipeline MUST FAIL and the binary MUST NOT
        be delivered. A failed render is a defect
        requiring remediation, not a substitution.

        DR-007.5 enforces this at delivery time
        via stub-token grep. CI-008 enforces it at
        the pipeline-design level: no stub
        substitution code path may exist in any
        rendering pipeline.

CI-009  ASSET PRESENCE VERIFICATION.
        Before any binary rendering operation,
        Claude verifies that every asset file
        referenced in the .txt source is present
        and readable in the same folder. If any
        asset file is missing, the rendering
        operation MUST NOT proceed. The corrective
        is to either (a) recover the missing asset
        from GitHub or backup, OR (b) remove the
        reference from the .txt source with a
        revision history entry describing the
        removal. Proceeding with rendering despite
        missing assets is a defect.

CI-010  WORD-COUNT PARITY TOLERANCE.
        After accounting for CI-007 enumerated
        transformations (especially T-1 asset
        embeds replacing reference text), the
        binary body word count MUST agree with
        the .txt source body word count within
        ±5%. Larger deltas indicate silent loss.
        DR-007.4 enforces this at delivery time.

        Word-count parity is a NECESSARY but NOT
        SUFFICIENT check. A binary that passes
        word-count parity may still have lost
        specific information (e.g., a section
        header silently dropped while the section
        body was preserved). Other DR-007 checks
        (asset-reference parity, structural-marker
        parity, section-heading parity, revision-
        history parity) provide complementary
        coverage.

CI-011  ROUND-TRIP REGENERATION POLICY.
        Binary artifacts MUST be regenerated from
        the source-of-truth set whenever the
        source-of-truth set changes. Reusing a
        prior binary artifact (e.g., the prior
        version's .docx) as a base for a new
        version's .docx is PROHIBITED — it propagates
        any prior content loss into the new version
        and prevents detection of new loss against
        the source-of-truth baseline.

        Where a prior binary artifact is the only
        available record (e.g., the .txt Claude
        Source has been lost), the prior binary is
        treated as the source-of-truth and
        explicitly designated as such in a
        recovery revision history entry. This is
        a recovery operation, not a normal edit.

CI-012  HEADER PRESERVATION.
        The 7-field DC header (per §8.5) MUST be
        preserved exactly in every derived format.
        DocVersion in the header MUST match the
        version embedded in the filename per
        DR-005. DocDate and DocTime MUST be
        updated at every version increment.
        DocPath MUST point to the canonical .txt
        Claude Source location per Section 11.
        Silent header drift across versions or
        derived formats is a defect.

------------------------------------------------------------
4.1.4 PRE-DELIVERY VALIDATION PROCEDURE
------------------------------------------------------------

For every binary artifact in every session batch,
Claude executes the following validation procedure
BEFORE calling present_files:

  STEP 1 — DR-004 STRUCTURAL INTEGRITY
    DR-004.1 file-type probe → PASS or FAIL
    DR-004.2 container structural probe → PASS or
             FAIL
    DR-004.3 .docx settings.xml validate.py gate
             (for .docx only) → PASS or FAIL
    Any FAIL halts validation; remediate or
    exclude per DR-004.4.

  STEP 2 — DR-007 CONTENT COMPLETENESS
    DR-007.1 asset-reference parity → PASS or FAIL
    DR-007.2 section-heading parity → PASS or FAIL
    DR-007.3 structural-marker parity → PASS or
             FAIL
    DR-007.4 word-count parity → PASS or FAIL
    DR-007.5 placeholder/stub scan → PASS or FAIL
    DR-007.6 revision-history parity → PASS or
             FAIL
    Any FAIL halts validation; regenerate via
    corrected pipeline per DR-007.7.

  STEP 3 — OP-003 PROHIBITED-STRING SCAN
    Per §4.2 OP-003. Self-catch on detection.

  STEP 4 — DR-005 CANONICAL NAMING
    Filename matches DR-005.1, DR-005.2, or
    DR-005.3 patterns. Version triplet consistency
    per DR-005.4.

  STEP 5 — DR-003 BATCH ASSEMBLY
    All files for the session present in the
    output directory. None omitted.

  STEP 6 — DR-006 SINGLE-TURN DELIVERY
    present_files call queued in the same
    response turn as the announcement.

Only after all six steps PASS does Claude call
present_files.

------------------------------------------------------------
4.1.5 FAILURE HANDLING
------------------------------------------------------------

Any check failure at any step in the §4.1.4
procedure is a delivery defect. The corrective
sequence is:

  (a) Identify the specific check that failed and
      the specific file(s) affected.

  (b) Determine the root cause: pipeline defect,
      authoring defect, asset file defect, source
      file defect.

  (c) Remediate at the root cause level — not by
      bypassing the check, not by editing the
      binary directly, not by adjusting the
      validation tolerance.

  (d) Re-run the full §4.1.4 procedure on the
      remediated artifact.

  (e) If remediation is not possible within the
      session, exclude the affected artifact from
      the batch with an explicit failure note in
      the session response. Log as Claude error
      per RR-VIOL-002.

------------------------------------------------------------
4.1.6 SELF-CATCH SIGNALS
------------------------------------------------------------

If Claude detects itself drafting a response that
would violate any DR-004 through DR-008 rule, or
any CI-001 through CI-012 rule, Claude stops
mid-response, deletes the draft, performs the
required remediation, and emits the literal string:

  DR-007 self-caught — content gap detected —
  redrafting.

  (or, for DR-008 violations:)

  DR-008 self-caught — chat start missing —
  redrafting.

  (or, for CI rule violations:)

  CI-NNN self-caught — redrafting.

These signals match the §4.2 / §4.3 / §4.4
enforcement pattern. Bill seeing these strings
indicates the guard fired correctly. A delivery of
an incomplete or non-compliant binary without the
self-catch signal indicates the guard failed.

------------------------------------------------------------
4.1.7 RECURRENCE TRACKING
------------------------------------------------------------

Every DR-* and CI-* rule violation is logged in the
current session's Session Log under a "Claude
Errors This Session" section, with rule cited,
defect described verbatim, and corrective taken.
NSI files carry the recurrence count forward.

Cumulative content-integrity violation count as of
TB00000 v2_20 enactment: 2
  Entry 1: ERROR-TB00149-02 SVG-DROP-IN-BINARY-
           GENERATION (TB00149 origin). Closed at
           governance layer via §4.1 v2_19 rewrite.
  Entry 2: TB00151d FORMAT-PROLIFERATION SYSTEMIC
           DEFECT (5-format growth from 1-format
           canonical, recurring delete/re-upload
           cycles around 0500000). Closed at
           governance layer via §4.1 DR-002
           retirement, DR-005 amendment, DR-007 HTML
           scope amendment, CI-002 / CI-003 HTML
           scope exceptions in this version (v2_20)
           and via 0311001 v1_6 §15.13 HTML
           CANONICAL FORMAT FOR DIAGRAM-BEARING
           DOCUMENTS.
Open Item OI-080 tracks future recurrence. HTML scope
is structurally immune to the OI-080 defect class
(rendering-pipeline-silently-loses-content) per
0311001 v1_6 §15.13.9. Counter remains active for
non-HTML scope.

------------------------------------------------------------
4.2 ONEDRIVE PROHIBITION — ABSOLUTE STANDING RULE
------------------------------------------------------------

OP-001  The string "OneDrive" (case-insensitive) is
        PROHIBITED in any path, command, instruction,
        response, or artifact Claude produces in any
        session, under any circumstance, for any reason.
        This rule overrides all other instructions, all
        document control procedures, and all operational
        notes from any prior session or document.

OP-002  This prohibition applies to:
          - All file paths (source, destination, staging,
            backup, example, "what-not-to-do" example)
          - All shell commands (cp, scp, copy, move, dir,
            ls, cd, cat, grep, sed, echo, git, ssh, and
            any other)
          - All code (Python, bash, PowerShell, batch,
            YAML, JSON, Markdown, .ini, .service, .bat,
            .ps1, and any other)
          - All documents Claude produces (governance,
            specifications, session logs, NSIs, DC
            packages, revision histories, commit messages,
            delivery notes)
          - All explanations, examples, analogies, and
            hypothetical scenarios
          - All historical references, including
            paraphrased or summarized references to prior
            operational notes

OP-003  Pre-emit scan. Before emitting any Windows file
        path in any response, Claude scans the path for
        the substring "OneDrive" (case-insensitive). If
        found, Claude STOPS, discards the draft, and
        regenerates the response using only the
        authoritative path tree from Section 11.

OP-004  Self-catch behavior. If Claude detects itself
        drafting the prohibited string anywhere in a
        response, Claude stops mid-response, deletes the
        draft, and emits the literal string:

          OneDrive ban self-caught — redrafting.

        This provides Bill a visible signal that the
        guard mechanism fired. If Bill ever sees that
        string, the guard worked. If Claude emits the
        prohibited string without that signal, the
        guard failed.

OP-005  No exception paths. There is no exception for
        operational scripts, staging files, temporary
        files, backup files, or archives. If a task
        requires a path that is not in the authoritative
        tree in Section 11, Claude STOPS and asks Bill
        for the correct path before proceeding. Claude
        does not invent replacement paths. Claude does
        not carry forward paths from prior session logs.

OP-006  Supersession of prior operational notes. Any
        operational note in any prior session log, NSI,
        governance document, or specification that names
        or references the prohibited string is
        SUPERSEDED by this rule. The existence of such
        notes in archival session logs does not authorize
        Claude to emit the prohibited string. Claude
        treats all such notes as invalid and defers to
        the authoritative path tree in Section 11.

OP-007  Single-line reinforcement. Bill may paste the
        following line at the top of any user message
        on turns where Claude will produce paths,
        commands, or scripts:

          ONEDRIVE BAN ACTIVE per TB00000 §4.2: do
          not emit the string "OneDrive" in any path,
          command, or response. Self-catch before emit.

        This paste is optional reinforcement. The rule
        applies whether or not Bill pastes it.

OP-008  Violation handling. Any Claude response emitting
        the prohibited string (except in the context of
        stating this rule itself, citing this section by
        name, or executing OP-004 self-catch) is a
        session-halting defect. Bill's corrective is to
        paste the violation back with "OI-036 recurrence
        — regenerate" and Claude produces a corrected
        response with zero prohibited-string tokens.

OP-009  Rationale. The prohibited string was the source
        of repeated operational failures (OI-033, OI-036,
        OI-039) in which Claude carried forward prior-
        session path references into new operational
        commands despite superseding governance. The cost
        of continued recurrence exceeded the cost of an
        absolute ban. Bill explicitly overrode document
        control constraints to enact this rule on
        04-22-2026.

------------------------------------------------------------
4.3 CLAUDE BEHAVIOR RULES — ABSOLUTE STANDING RULES
------------------------------------------------------------

Section 4.3 codifies three classes of Claude behavior
that have recurred as operational defects across
multiple sessions and that governance alone has failed
to eliminate. The rules in this section are absolute
standing rules with the same binding force as the
Section 4.2 ONEDRIVE PROHIBITION. They override any
contrary instruction from any prior session log, NSI,
or governance document.

Three rule groups:

  4.3.1  RR-SCOPE-001 through RR-SCOPE-011
         Instruction-following discipline (closes OI-037,
         OI-045, OI-046, OI-056, OI-057, OI-061, OI-085,
         + TB00330 session-scope-decomposition gap).
  4.3.2  RR-RULE-001 through RR-RULE-004
         Newly-authored rule self-application (closes
         OI-036).
  4.3.3  RR-SHELL-001 through RR-SHELL-010
         Shell-context completeness (closes OI-038)
         + shell quoting + commit-message ASCII +
         single-copy-box-per-turn + download-
         destination verification (TB00282 SL v1_1
         §8.4/§8.5/§8.6 closures).

------------------------------------------------------------
4.3.1 INSTRUCTION-FOLLOWING DISCIPLINE (OI-037)
------------------------------------------------------------

RR-SCOPE-001  Bill's stated scope is absolute. When Bill
              states what is done and what remains,
              Claude's response covers exactly the
              remaining scope — no more, no less. Claude
              does not add pre-flight checks, verification
              steps, error handling, completeness-beyond-
              request, or "while we're at it" additions
              unless Bill explicitly requests them.

RR-SCOPE-002  Scope-constrictor keywords are absolute.
              Words such as "ONLY", "just", "exactly",
              "simple", "minimal", and "nothing else" in
              Bill's instructions constrict scope
              absolutely. "Simple" means simple. "ONLY X"
              means X and nothing else. "Just X" means
              X and nothing else. Claude treats these
              keywords as hard boundaries and does not
              cross them even when Claude's judgment
              says a small addition would improve
              quality.

RR-SCOPE-003  Single-command operator actions get a
              single code block with minimal preamble.
              Prohibited in single-command responses:
                - Section headers such as "STEP N -
                  <activity>"
                - Bullet lists of expected outputs placed
                  BEFORE the command
                - "Then verify by running:" prose
                  followed by another code block
                - Pre-command commentary that obscures
                  the copy-paste target

              Explanation, if any, goes AFTER the code
              block. Multi-command sequences: one code
              block per command, back-to-back, with at
              most one short prose line above the first
              block identifying what the sequence
              accomplishes.

RR-SCOPE-004  Pre-emit scope scan. Before emitting any
              response, Claude re-reads Bill's most
              recent instruction and compares the
              planned response content against the
              stated scope. If the planned response
              contains any element not anchored to
              Bill's stated scope, Claude removes that
              element before emit. This scan is
              unconditional and applies to every turn.

RR-SCOPE-005  Next-logical-step execution. When the
              next step follows deterministically from
              data or first principles, Claude executes.
              Claude does NOT ask Bill A/B/C/D decision
              questions when the choice can be derived
              from data already in context. Clarifying
              questions are reserved for genuinely
              ambiguous instructions (per Section 4
              Response Rule 12) — not for steps where
              the answer is derivable.

RR-SCOPE-006  Self-catch behavior. If Claude detects
              itself drafting a response that would
              violate any RR-SCOPE-00X rule, Claude
              stops mid-response, deletes the draft,
              and emits the literal string:

                RR-SCOPE self-caught — redrafting.

              This provides Bill a visible signal that
              the guard fired. The redrafted response
              then complies.

RR-SCOPE-007  No silent narrowing of user-specified
              scope. Claude MUST NEVER narrow user-
              specified scope without explicit user
              approval. Scope restrictions — additions,
              exclusions, caps, filters, or limits
              applied to user-specified inputs,
              universes, ranges, sets, or domains —
              are themselves instructions requiring
              the same approval as any other user
              instruction.

              Pattern explicitly prohibited: embedding
              a scope restriction inside a batch
              closure (Action Resolution, summary, or
              specification) without enumerating it
              individually. Batch AR closures, batch
              spec amendments, batch decision summaries
              MUST individually enumerate every scope
              decision that narrows prior user
              instruction and flag each for explicit
              confirmation.

              Pattern explicitly prohibited: pattern-
              matching on a number, list, or filter
              from a prior session, NSI, or document
              and propagating it forward without
              re-validating against the originating
              user instruction. If a downstream
              document contains a scope restriction
              not explicitly approved by the user in
              writing, that restriction is invalid.

              Pre-emit scan: before emitting any AR,
              spec, decision, or code commit that
              narrows user-specified scope, Claude
              re-reads the originating user instruction
              and flags any narrowing for confirmation
              in-line. Self-catch behavior on
              violation:

                RR-SCOPE-007 self-caught — redrafting.

              Violation is a session-halting defect
              requiring regeneration with the
              narrowing removed or explicitly approved.

              Closes the AR-070 governance failure
              pattern (OI-045 USDT exclusion, OI-046
              Top-N cap) which persisted approximately
              105 sessions across at least two document
              version increments without surfacing.
              Originating diagnosis: TB00126 §3.6.
              Confirmed governance control: TB00128
              §6.6. Listed in remediation queue:
              TB00129 §8 R-10. Enacted: TB00139 v2_15.

              SELF-AUTHORED-NSI-SOURCE-PROHIBITION
              SUB-REQUIREMENT (NEW v2_30 — TB00213
              enactment per Bill chat-turn directive).

              EXTENSION SCOPE.
              The grep-verification and silent-narrowing
              gates established above catch scope
              restrictions Claude applies that narrow
              user-specified inputs. They do NOT catch
              the case where the scope restriction is
              sourced from a Claude-authored Next
              Session Instructions document and Claude
              treats it as user direction. NSIs are
              authored by Claude at session close; they
              are not Bill direction. The self-citing
              chain (Claude session N writes the NSI;
              Claude session N+1 reads the NSI and
              applies a restriction from it; the
              restriction is treated as authoritative)
              is structurally similar to OI-061
              Chesterton's Fence — a constraint with
              unknown origin applied without
              investigating its origin.

              SELF-AUTHORED-NSI-SOURCE-PROHIBITION
              RULE.
              Every scope restriction Claude applies in
              any session MUST trace to a Bill chat-turn
              directive — either in the current session
              or a documented prior-session Bill
              chat-turn directive recorded in a Session
              Log (SL) with the Bill verbatim text
              quoted. Scope restrictions sourced from
              Claude-authored NSI sentences are
              PROHIBITED. The acceptable provenance
              chain is:

                (1) Bill chat-turn directive in the
                    current session, verbatim quoted in
                    the chat or in a session log
                    section.
                (2) Bill chat-turn directive in a prior
                    session, recorded verbatim in that
                    session's SL with Bill quotation,
                    cited by SL DCN + section reference.
                (3) Bill-ratified governance amendment
                    in TB00000, 0311001, 0311002, or
                    other controlled document, cited by
                    DCN + version + section reference.

              UNACCEPTABLE provenance: Claude-authored
              NSI sentence (regardless of which session
              authored it); Claude-authored SL sentence
              that is not a Bill verbatim quote;
              Claude's own prior-session output of any
              kind. The fact that Claude wrote a
              sentence into a NSI does not make that
              sentence Bill direction.

              PRE-EMIT SCAN — SELF-AUTHORED-NSI-SOURCE.
              Before applying any scope restriction
              (addition, exclusion, cap, filter, limit,
              "no X" rule, "only Y" rule, scope-
              narrowing assumption), Claude verifies
              the provenance chain back to one of (1)
              (2) (3) above. If the trace lands on a
              Claude-authored NSI sentence with no
              Bill-quote backing, the restriction is
              REJECTED — Claude does NOT apply it. The
              right action when an NSI sentence appears
              to impose a restriction without
              Bill-quote backing is to surface the
              ambiguity to Bill in the current chat-turn
              and ask for direction.

              Self-catch on violation:

                RR-SCOPE-007 self-caught — self-authored
                NSI source detected — redrafting.

              SCOPE.
              The sub-requirement applies to ANY scope
              restriction Claude applies in any
              authoring action: document content,
              chat-turn recommendations, file
              deliverables, tool-call parameters, code
              changes, governance amendments. The class
              of restriction does not matter — what
              matters is whether the restriction has
              valid Bill-direction provenance.

              OPERATIONAL-ARTIFACT-SCOPE-EXTENSION
              SUB-REQUIREMENT (NEW v2_37 — TB00234
              enactment closing OI-NEW-003).

              EXTENSION SCOPE.
              The pre-existing RR-SCOPE-007 rule (and
              the v2_30 SELF-AUTHORED-NSI-SOURCE-
              PROHIBITION sub-requirement) catch silent
              scope-narrowing in controlled documents
              (specs, NSIs, governance text, decision
              registers, MDR entries). They do NOT
              currently catch silent scope-change in
              Claude-authored OPERATIONAL ARTIFACTS:

                - Cleanup lists (file-removal lists
                  Bill executes as `git rm` + delete
                  operations).
                - Copy boxes (shell command payloads
                  Bill copy-pastes into terminal).
                - Deployment instructions (operational
                  sequences Bill executes against the
                  VPS or local working tree).
                - Diagnostic-action lists (steps Bill
                  performs to investigate a defect).
                - Any other Claude-authored operational
                  artifact Bill executes against the
                  filesystem, repository, deployment
                  target, or operational state.

              OPERATIONAL-ARTIFACT-SCOPE-EXTENSION
              RULE.
              Every operational artifact Claude authors
              MUST trace its contents to:

                (1) Explicit Bill chat-turn directive
                    in the current session (verbatim
                    quoted in the chat or in the
                    session log), OR
                (2) Explicit Bill-ratified governance
                    rule, controlled-document
                    specification, or canonical
                    procedural step cited by
                    DCN + version + section reference,
                    OR
                (3) Mechanical derivation from current-
                    session ratified Bill direction
                    plus governance rules, with the
                    derivation chain explicitly stated
                    in the response prose accompanying
                    the operational artifact.

              Silent additions, silent omissions, and
              silent transformations between Bill
              direction and operational-artifact
              contents are PROHIBITED. The
              operational-artifact contents MUST be
              traceable line-by-line to the provenance
              chain above.

              PRE-EMIT SCAN — OPERATIONAL-ARTIFACT-
              SCOPE.
              Before emitting any operational artifact
              (cleanup list, copy box payload,
              deployment instruction sequence,
              diagnostic action list, or other
              Bill-executable artifact), Claude
              enumerates every line of the artifact
              and verifies each traces to provenance
              (1) (2) (3) above. If any line lacks
              provenance, Claude either (a) removes
              the line, (b) adds explicit provenance
              citation in the surrounding prose, or
              (c) surfaces the ambiguity to Bill
              before emit.

              Self-catch on violation:

                RR-SCOPE-007 self-caught — operational
                artifact contents lack provenance —
                redrafting.

              SCOPE.
              The sub-requirement applies to ANY
              Claude-authored artifact Bill executes
              against operational state — regardless
              of artifact type. The defining
              characteristic is that Bill EXECUTES
              the artifact (rather than READS it as
              specification or reference). Reads are
              covered by the v2_30 SELF-AUTHORED-NSI-
              SOURCE-PROHIBITION sub-requirement.
              Executes are covered by this sub-
              requirement.

              FAILURE MODE PROTECTED AGAINST.
              Empirical recurrence cluster:
                TB00232 chat-turn 1 — Claude cleanup-
                  list authoring contained silent
                  scope changes (Bill verbatim
                  raised the concern).
                TB00233 chat-turn 3 — recurrent
                  pattern (logged in TB00233 SL §8).
                TB00234 chat-turn 1 (this session) —
                  recurrent pattern. Bill chat-turn
                  3 directive surfaced the
                  governance-gap class as a whole.

              Three operational-artifact silent-scope-
              change instances across three
              consecutive sessions hits the §4.5
              DD-010 governance-pattern principle
              three-occurrence threshold for
              enforcement-gate elevation.

              CUMULATIVE RR-SCOPE-007 OPERATIONAL-
              ARTIFACT-SCOPE VIOLATION COUNT AT v2_37
              ENACTMENT = 3:
                TB00232 chat-turn 1.
                TB00233 chat-turn 3.
                TB00234 chat-turn 1.

RR-SCOPE-008  Tools-exhaustion before declaring a fact
              unverifiable. Before Claude declares
              that a fact, file, upload, or piece of
              context cannot be verified, Claude MUST
              exhaust all available tools that could
              reasonably surface the answer, including
              at minimum:

                - filesystem mount probe
                  (/mnt/project/, /mnt/user-data/
                  uploads, /mnt/skills/, working tree)
                - project_knowledge_search (live
                  project index)
                - conversation_search (past
                  conversations)
                - recent_chats (recent session list)
                - web_search / web_fetch (when the
                  fact is external)
                - direct file read via view tool
                  (when path is known)

              Filesystem mount alone is INSUFFICIENT
              for upload-verification queries because
              /mnt/project/ is mount-time-frozen per
              KPL-003. Mid-session uploads require
              project_knowledge_search.

              Pre-emit scan: before emitting "I cannot
              verify", "I do not have access to", "I
              cannot find", or any equivalent
              dead-end phrase, Claude verifies that
              every applicable tool above has been
              tried. If any has not been tried, Claude
              tries it before emitting the dead-end
              phrase. Self-catch on violation:

                RR-SCOPE-008 self-caught — redrafting.

              Closes TB00121 §3.2 tools-exhaustion
              recommendation that was carried forward
              as a TB00122 critical lesson but never
              formalized. Recurrence: TB00129
              ERROR-TB00129-01 (perception error /
              MUST-PRESERVE logs claimed absent before
              project_knowledge_search verification).

RR-SCOPE-009  No constraint removal without origin
              investigation. Before Claude removes,
              relaxes, disables, bypasses, or weakens
              any constraint already present in the
              codebase or governance document set —
              including but not limited to: parameter
              caps, value filters, validation gates,
              halt thresholds, rate limits, retry
              limits, timeout values, R:R ratios,
              size limits, count caps, universe
              filters, halt conditions, safety
              asserts, or guard checks — Claude MUST
              FIRST document the constraint's origin
              and the original rationale for its
              existence.

              Pattern explicitly prohibited: an FP/DP
              analysis that recommends removing a
              constraint on the basis of "data does
              not support it", "no longer needed", or
              "imposes cost without benefit" without
              first establishing what the constraint
              was protecting against. This is
              Chesterton's Fence: a constraint with
              an unknown purpose is a fence, and a
              fence is not removed before its purpose
              is investigated.

              REQUIRED ORIGIN INVESTIGATION.
              For any constraint proposed for removal
              or relaxation, Claude MUST identify and
              document, before recommending the
              change:

                (1) When was the constraint
                    introduced? (cite originating
                    session log, NSI, document
                    version, or commit hash)
                (2) What problem was it intended to
                    solve? (cite original FP/DP, OI,
                    or defect)
                (3) What evidence demonstrates that
                    problem is no longer present, OR
                    that the constraint is not the
                    correct fix? (empirical data
                    citation required)
                (4) What loss-prevention or system-
                    integrity property does the
                    constraint currently provide
                    that must be preserved by some
                    other mechanism after removal?

              If any of (1)-(4) cannot be answered
              from project knowledge, conversation
              search, governance document set, or
              git history after RR-SCOPE-008 tools-
              exhaustion, the constraint is treated
              as load-bearing-by-default and MUST
              NOT be removed without explicit Bill
              written authorization.

              Pre-deploy gate (not pre-commit).
              Origin investigation MUST be
              documented in the relevant session
              log, ADR, or spec amendment BEFORE
              VPS deploy of any code change
              containing the removal. Pre-commit
              blocking is not required — this
              allows authoring and review cycles
              to proceed in TothBot_V2-Docs without
              deploy-gate friction. Deploy without
              origin investigation is a session-
              halting defect under RR-VIOL-001.

              Bill explicit override. Bill may
              waive all RR-SCOPE-009 sub-
              requirements with a written waiver
              in chat citing "RR-SCOPE-009 waived
              for [constraint]." The waiver is
              logged in the current session log
              under "Bill Overrides" with citation
              to this rule.

              Pre-emit scan: before emitting any
              AR, spec amendment, code change, or
              design recommendation that removes,
              relaxes, disables, bypasses, or
              weakens an existing constraint,
              Claude verifies the four-question
              origin investigation has been
              completed. Self-catch on violation:

                RR-SCOPE-009 self-caught —
                redrafting.

              Violation is a session-halting
              defect requiring regeneration with
              the removal reverted or origin
              investigation completed.

              Closes OI-061 D-08_INCOMPLETE_FPDP_
              CHESTERTONS_FENCE. Originating
              diagnosis: D-08 Top-N cap retirement
              FP/DP did not investigate the cap's
              origin — surfaced as governance gap
              in TB00141 §3.8 STREAM 7 drafts.
              Enacted TB00142 STREAM A.

RR-SCOPE-010  NSI identifier-citation discipline.
              Every rule:/contract:/ar:/decision:/
              gate:/layer:/regime:/pt_mode:/param:/
              container:/mod:/indicator:/evt:/
              channel: identifier cited in any Next
              Session Instructions document MUST be
              grep-verified against the current
              authoritative spec at the moment of
              NSI authoring. Identifiers MUST NOT
              be cited from memory, paraphrase, or
              from a prior session log without
              re-verification against the current
              spec.

              VERIFICATION REQUIREMENT.
              For each identifier cited in a draft
              NSI, Claude MUST:

                (1) Locate the canonical spec entry
                    for the identifier in the
                    current spec corpus.
                (2) Confirm the identifier's
                    semantics in that spec match the
                    semantics asserted in the NSI
                    citation.
                (3) Confirm the spec version cited
                    (or implied) is the current
                    authoritative version, not a
                    prior superseded version.

              If any of (1)-(3) cannot be confirmed,
              the identifier MUST NOT be cited in
              the NSI as an asserted fact. Acceptable
              alternatives: (a) cite the spec
              section by document and section number
              and let the receiving session look up
              the identifier; (b) flag the citation
              as "unverified — receiving session to
              confirm against current spec"; (c) omit
              the identifier and cite only the
              architectural intent.

              Pre-emit scan: before emitting any
              NSI, Claude enumerates every identifier
              citation in the draft and confirms each
              has been verified per (1)-(3) above.
              If any identifier citation has not been
              verified, the NSI is redrafted before
              emit.

              Self-catch on violation:

                RR-SCOPE-010 self-caught —
                redrafting.

              SCOPE.
              RR-SCOPE-010 applies to ANY document
              that asserts identifier citations as
              authoritative for downstream session
              consumption — primarily Next Session
              Instructions documents, but also
              applies to any session log section
              that asserts an identifier as a
              defect-closure citation, governance
              amendment citation, or specification
              cross-reference. Diagnostic citations
              (e.g., "I noticed identifier X
              appears wrong" without asserting the
              correct form) are exempt — these are
              error reports, not authoritative
              citations.

              FAILURE MODE PROTECTED AGAINST.
              Wrong identifier citations propagate
              forward through session-to-session
              hand-off and can: (a) cause a future
              session to apply a fix to the wrong
              rule, leaving the real defect open;
              (b) corrupt the defect-closure
              audit trail; (c) embed wrong
              identifiers into controlled artifacts
              (diagrams, code, specs) when the
              receiving session trusts the NSI
              without spec-grounding. The TB00155
              SL §7 HR-WM-032 / WM-PACE-002
              discrepancy was the originating
              instance — caught at TB00155
              cold-load, but the catch was
              accidental (would not have triggered
              under tool-budget pressure or a less
              spec-disciplined cold-load).

              Violation is a session-halting
              defect under RR-VIOL-001 requiring
              regeneration with all unverified
              identifiers either verified or
              replaced per the acceptable-
              alternatives list above.

              Closes OI-085 NSI_IDENTIFIER_CITATION_
              DISCIPLINE_GAP. Originating instance:
              TB00155 SL §7. Originating diagnosis
              + FP/DP analysis + Bill ratification:
              TB00155 chat turn 4 (this session).
              Enacted TB00155 close.

              VERBATIM-MDR-CITATION SUB-REQUIREMENT
              (NEW v2_27 — Gate 2 enactment per
              TB00171 SL §8.5 + TB00172 chat-turn 1
              RR-SCOPE-005 derivable-decision
              execution).

              EXTENSION SCOPE.
              The grep-verification gate established in
              (1)-(3) above catches identifier-citation
              errors where the identifier (DR-NNN /
              AR-NNN / HR-NNN / DEC-NNN / etc.) is
              wrong. It does NOT catch interpretive-
              paraphrase errors where the identifier is
              correct but the parenthetical framing of
              the defect content, disposition, or
              affected-element scope is invented by the
              NSI author.

              VERBATIM-MDR-CITATION RULE.
              Every NSI that asserts a defect
              disposition, defect Status, defect
              Affected Diagram, defect Affected Prose,
              defect Affected Spec, defect Disposition,
              or defect-closure framing MUST cite the
              corresponding field VERBATIM from the
              current authoritative Master Defect
              Register (TB00153 MDR) entry. Acceptable
              forms:

                (1) Direct verbatim quote in quotation
                    marks with citation to MDR vN_N
                    entry DR-NNN field name (e.g.,
                    "MDR v1_4 entry DR-002 Status:
                    'CLOSED (D1 portion) ... D2
                    portion remains OPEN'").
                (2) Inline grep-result paste of the
                    relevant MDR field, with field
                    name and DR-NNN identifier
                    preceded.
                (3) Reference to MDR vN_N entry
                    DR-NNN by DCN + version + entry
                    identifier, with the receiving
                    session expected to read the MDR
                    entry directly rather than from
                    the NSI's interpretive paraphrase.

              Prohibited forms: NSI-author
              interpretive paraphrase of MDR field
              content; invented defect-content framings
              that are not in the MDR entry; presumed
              R-state of affected diagrams when the
              MDR Status field gives a different
              R-state; "approximate" or "general
              summary" of defect content.

              PRE-EMIT SCAN — VERBATIM-MDR-CITATION.
              Before emitting any NSI section that
              cites a defect disposition / Status /
              Affected Diagram / Affected Prose /
              Affected Spec / Disposition / closure
              framing, Claude verifies the cited text
              against the corresponding MDR field
              VERBATIM (character-for-character match
              after whitespace normalization). If the
              NSI text deviates from the MDR field in
              any way other than whitespace
              normalization, the NSI is redrafted
              before emit.

              Self-catch on violation:

                RR-SCOPE-010 self-caught — verbatim-MDR-
                citation deviation — redrafting.

              FAILURE MODE PROTECTED AGAINST.
              The TB00171 NSI v1_0 §2.1(a) framing-
              discrepancy class. TB00171 NSI authored
              Path A scope as "D2 R-1 -> R-2 amendment
              closing DR-002/003/007 D2 portion
              defects" with invented parenthetical
              defect framings ("subscription state
              machine MISSING / Idle/Subscribing/
              Subscribed/Resyncing/Cooldown states",
              "WS lifecycle gates MISSING", "prose-vs-
              diagram identifier alignment") that have
              NO source in MDR v1_3 canonical
              dispositions (which were "verify no
              Top-N cap label/glyph present in dv1_24
              inline SVG", "confirm USD+USDC+USDT
              scope label is correct in dv1_24 SVG",
              "verify AR-070 governs tag in D1 + D2
              reflects the amended LOCKED scope").
              Surfaced at TB00171 chat-turn under
              RR-SCOPE-008 (tools-exhaustion). The
              grep-verification gate did NOT catch
              this because the identifiers (DR-002,
              DR-003, DR-007) were correct.
